but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料如何運作 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解、使用的東西最後會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿的衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直是微乎其微的燃料 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當他們發表一篇論文時 , 用比較簡單的方法製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他對化學一無所知 , 直到那時 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間中進行實驗 , 只用了現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用他自己的旋渦混合器 , 根據另一位科學家/製造師的教導 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦接著在網路上發表了他的研究結果 , 包括他曾經嘗試過的所有東西 , 且沒有用 , 讓其他人可以研究並重製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦主要的創新形式 , 是把一個實驗用在大學裡的有裝備的實驗室裡 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重現 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 他自己製造出來 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程 , 改進 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個我想要提到她的計畫目標的例子是強調材料的表達特質 , 同時把焦點放在建造者的創意和技巧上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子組件非常強大 , 他們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但在他們的設計中 , 限制與生俱來的影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面漢娜的作法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 使我們免於預先設計的限制 , 藉由教導我們材料本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有銅膠帶連結到mp3播放器和磁鐵
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的馬賽洛柯爾荷研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電的布料和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造家一樣 , 漢娜出版了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都可以複製、繁殖它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的工藝作品 , 以及她共同發現的事實 , 打開了一連串新的可能性 , 這些可能都是美感上訴和創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以製造家有趣的地方在於我們從熱情和好奇心中創造出來 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常處理非傳統角度的問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人用材料做實驗 , 研究人員就越願意分享他們的研究 , 製造出他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正能服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主體 , 只有科學家在關心 , 沒有人夢想能在家中做一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先前知識 , 是確保我們在未來有發言權的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡泡 , 鎖住門 , 按下加速器 , 依靠我們的眼睛來指導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面和後面那些車子 。 但如果車子能彼此分享資料 , 了解它們的位置和速度 , 並用預測模型來計算路上每個人最安全的路線 ? jeniferhealy想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛healey:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能會避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車很危險 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的事情之一 , 但是宗教圖像和好運魅力出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛著我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是十六到十九歲美國人死亡的主要原因 , 導致死亡的原因和百分之七十五的意外沒有任何關係毒品或酒精 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能肯定 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是個年輕的司機 , 在高速公路上 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈繼續下去 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這個傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不是在放慢速度 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停下來 , 停下來 , 停在高速公路上
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛剛到65歲到零了 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在煞車上撞了一下 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感受到abs踢進去 , 車子還在 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 車子全都被安裝了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到車停了 , 我想我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以轉變開車的體驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只希望各位能稍微思考一下開車的體驗是什麼樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 。 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 ,
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導向部分看不見的道路 , 在其他金屬巨人之中 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 而你只需要指導你是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 眼睛不是真正為這個任務而設計的 , 但之後人們要求你做一些事情 , 像是 , 你想做一條車道改變 , 他們問你做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿掉 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車下去 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是開車的安全方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看這邊還是我看這邊 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一份很棒的工作挑選 , 選擇我們在路上要做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過某件事 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到錯或遲到 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 , 我相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 有了車輛互相交換資料 , 我們將能看到不只是前面三輛車 , 還有三輛車後面 , 往右和左邊 , 全都同時 , 鳥瞰視野 , 我們將能夠真正的看到那些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙走了多快或停止了多遠 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我會知道
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為那是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 那真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 。 用汽車 , 這不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是有固定位置和速度的三維物體 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路行駛 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在出版前的路線上行駛 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於在不遠的將來 , 要做出合理的預測 , 並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在你的車上 , 一些摩托車騎機車來了 ! 時速85英哩 , 車道插座--我知道你有過這樣的經驗 , 不是那個傢伙從無處不在 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙大概在前半小時都在路上
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英哩後 , 有人看到那個傢伙 , 一旦有車看到那個傢伙 , 把他放到地圖上 , 他在地圖上的位置 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英里的速度持續下去 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你就會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那輛車會在他耳邊低語 , 比如說: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說相當不錯 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達到目的 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從一些簡單的東西開始 , 如同分享我們車子之間的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和一台攝影機在我的車裡 , 我有很精確的概念 , 知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子位置 , 有點像在哪裡 , 還有他們要去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車輛也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己身在何處 , 並且有點模糊地認識其他車子的位置 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車分享那些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以準確地告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	鮑勃.旺格教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當毛茸茸的估計結合時 , 甚至在光線交通上 , 當汽車只是分享gps資料 , 我們把這個研究從電腦模擬出來 , 移到機器人測試床上 , 這些裝在這些機器人身上的感測器:stereo攝影機、gps , 以及在後備系統中常見的二維雷射測器 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也附著一個分散的短距通訊電台 , 機器人會彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此來到時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們就能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在正在將越來越多的機器人加入混合當中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你得到太多的聊天 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 這就是預測模型幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子全都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會那麼注意那些包裹 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先考慮一個看起來有點偏離軌道的傢伙
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以預測新的軌跡
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他是怎麼走的 , 你知道怎麼走的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道你需要警告哪些駕駛者 , 才能脫身 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做怎麼能警告所有人的最好 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼能悄悄的說: 「 你需要走出去 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人真的有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能不是在緊急狀況中做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一系列的研究來做駕駛狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛是不是向前看 , 向下看 , 在電話上看 , 或是喝一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外狀況 , 我們可以預測誰、誰、哪輛車 , 都在最適合的位置 , 可以走出最適合的路徑 , 來為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 現今這些科技的存在
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常令人不安的想法 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 和其他車子聊天 , 我們會在一片八卦大海中走在路上 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看著你的車 , 我並不真的知道你是怎麼想的 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請你考慮一下 , 如果你真的不希望身後的青少年知道你在煞車 , 你要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做到最適合每個人的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車八卦關於你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金實現他前往太空的夢想 , 藉由一起飛行到上層的大氣中 , 並在零g中體驗到無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	企業、飛行、科學、簡短的演講、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在stephenhawking上以g0為主題
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	在座認識我的人都知道我有多麼熱衷於打開太空邊境 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給予世界重力專家--無重力的經驗--那真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 通過基因組學的考古獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個團隊在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一種叫做 「 基因體一百個個體 」 的基因組 , 我們就是其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特椅子就是那個事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力中 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 地球上唯一能體驗zerog的方法 , 其實是搭乘悖論飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 沒有體重25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再 , 再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8 , 10分鐘的無重力──太空總署如何訓練他們的太空人──多久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關 , 一家公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了那個人 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想要去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場媒體大會 , 我們宣佈我們的意圖要做一個zerog拋物面鏡 , 給他25秒的zerog 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼想上去做這個 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常動人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正不斷增加 , 遭受災難的風險......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果它不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在美國太空總署的飛行器內部 , 進入zerog飛機後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款我們募到15萬美元捐款給和我們一起飛翔的兒童慈善團體 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾位ted人
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個急診室
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液、心跳速率、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們把一切都設定在緊急情況下 ; 天知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 那裡的太空梭起飛 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴拜倫.里奇騰伯格和我小心地把他吊成0.
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們讓他去體驗無重力是真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物線之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說 , 去吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二次拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的在向艾薩克牛頓爵士致敬一顆蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋有同樣的椅子 , 伊薩克.牛頓也這麼做 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七名和第八名 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這位男子看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們有生之年 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這場史詩般的冒險
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫師davidbolinsky呈現出驚人的動畫 , 呈現出細胞內的緩衝生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫療、科學、科技、視覺化 ,
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我從稍微不同的觀點
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在觀察 , 自從我長大以來 , 藝術和真與美的表達方式和科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩件很棒的事都是在它們的右邊 , 它們都有很美妙的事物 , 會讓它們成為理想中的真與美 , 可以被科學和數學所檢視 , 幾乎就像是科學家會想要約會的理想雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相的表達方式是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是它們是你能崇拜的東西 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強而有力的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時是有用的 , 在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以翻些圖片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美往往對不在科學領域的人來說是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用一種形容美的事物 , 通常只能讓你了解語言 , 以及研究對象的語言和語法 , 來表達出真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 在那裡你會看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字進化而來 , 這些都是非常難理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導我的醫學插畫師以來 , 我試著要做的是 , 他是一位雕塑家 , 以及我的視覺導師 , 我想要找出一種方法 , 來幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 透過使用動畫 , 用圖像 , 說出故事 , 這樣人們不見得能被帶出來 , 且能被教導 , 且能被了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常都沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們所學到的 , 是受試者有真與美 , 他們被灌輸在其中 , 但他們被教導的方式是被拿來做比較 , 被歸結為事實和美麗不見得總是顯著的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 你把雞煮熟 , 直到香味剛不見 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我和哈佛大學的robertlue接到電話 , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 幾年前 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否會有興趣 , 且願意真正改變哈佛的醫學和科學教育是怎麼做的 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一項計畫 , 探索細胞 , 探索分子和細胞生物學中與生俱來的真與美 , 讓學生可以了解一個更大的圖片 , 可以把這些事實掛在上面 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以有一個心智圖像 , 視為一個大型、忙碌、非常複雜的城市 , 被微機械佔據著 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 世界各地都很羨慕奈米科技專家 , 他們自我引導、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 都是用一串胺基酸做成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械是如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	細胞如何複製 , 使我們的心臟充滿活力
they power our minds .	它們驅動了我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 找出我們如何把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 將是哈佛的生物visions的中心點 , 這個網站是哈佛大學為分子和細胞生物學的學生所設立的 , 除了所有的教科資訊之外 , 把所有教學內容都整合在一起 , 這樣這些學生就有了內化的看法 , 了解細胞的真與美 , 並且能夠研究這些想法 , 讓他們的想像力被激發出來 , 以至於他們將來 , 發現他們的新事物 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是 , 你有巨噬細胞 , 將它們串在微血管中 , 它們在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們從毛細管壁上的細胞取得資訊 , 它們被賦予了這個資訊 , 在外面的某處 , 有發炎 , 它們無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓他們停下來 , 造成他們內化 , 使他們需要製造所有各式各樣的零件 , 使他們改變自己的形狀 , 並試著脫離這個微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家和資料庫模型合作 , 找出原子上精確的分子 , 並找出它們如何移動 , 找出它們的做法 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何以真相為真 , 實現當時的狀況 , 但事實並非如此 , 細胞裡的擁擠會阻礙視覺的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一部三分鐘的讀者消化版我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是個持續進行的計劃 , 會再過四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看看細胞製造的路徑 , 這些小型步行機器 , 它們被稱為 「 kinesins 」 , 採用這些巨大的載量 , 用相對大小的螞蟻來挑戰 。
run the movie , please .	來執行電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器 , 真的相當驚人 , 它們是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞資訊 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內不同的事發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會真的製造它在果蠅所需的零件 , 從讀取基因的分子所帶來的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 都有可能沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 沒有這些機器 , 真的會讓出席 , 克里斯 , 真的很激烈 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex送貨員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 「 松果 」 , 他拉著一堆裝滿全新的製造蛋白質 , 到細胞中任何需要的位置 , 不論是裝在薄膜上 , 不論是裝在器官上 , 不論是用來製造東西或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	而我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西跑來跑去 , 現在 , 在你們的一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以不論你有多懶惰的感覺 , 你本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 回家後 , 我希望各位思考一下這件事 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	並思考一些我們正在學習的關於細胞力學的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞清楚了所有這些事情 , 相信我 , 一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們真的能夠對我們的健康有很大的控制權 , 用我們未來世代所做的事 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能夠用這個來發現更多真相 , 和更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 非常驚人的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經足夠意識到細胞需要它們的協助 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們同心協力 。 它們讓細胞做出它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們同心協力 , 協助我們的身體 , 巨大的實體 , 它們永遠無法正常地看見 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布朗頓計劃在她的旅行車上住了一年 , 看到了這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症開始 , 以及她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅程變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她形容她成為美國無家可歸者的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、說故事、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:我是無家可歸的那一年 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是個非常好奇的人 , 所以 , 身為記者 , 在22年間 , 我學會了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做一件事 , 就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了我身為報紙編輯的工作 , 在我父親在同年二月去世後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做時 , 我有很多事想要去感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我終其一生都在露營 。 然後我決定住在旅行車裡 , 要花一年時間做這件事 , 會像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓、我的旋轉推車和露營車都塞進了1975年雪佛蘭的車裡 , 開到日落裡 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:社會等同於生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一片粉碎 , 擁有一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒意識到 , 其他人的負面觀念能對我們的現實造成多快的影響 , 如果我們讓它發生 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒意識到無家可歸是種態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車上很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	而我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親的憤怒和憂鬱症出現了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 而我必須得到一份全職工作來支付這些帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個很溫和的春天變成很熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	而且在任何地方都不可能停車 , 不用很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過車廂的一扇開窗 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	小狗進入了日照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能夠 , 我都會在辦公大樓和卡車站使用員工淋浴間 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室清洗
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間在車廂裡的溫度很少降到華氏80度以下讓睡眠變得困難或無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我胸口的冰塊在數小時之內就融化了 , 相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找到一間公寓 , 或負擔不起一間公寓 , 能讓我有旋轉推車和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱能讓我太過病去走50英尺到旅行車外的公共廁所時 , 我在晚上用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天天氣進來時 , 溫度下降到冰凍之下 。 他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停在不一樣的地方 , 這樣我會避免被警察注意到 , 並且被困住 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感到自己無法掌控自己的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它是何時或如何發生的 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 到一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在旅行車裡 , 帶走我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒改變 。 我的智商尚未下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華 , 我的完整性 , 我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的一切都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我螺旋越來越深入到憂鬱症中 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 , 三天沒洗澡
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排在隊伍裡的人一樣瘦又沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或很高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當有幾個無家者意識到 , 包括前一所大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 , 你為什麼真的在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我有 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的反應讓我憂鬱症患者自殺 。 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•魯塞特 , 他是全國知名的記者 , 一直以來都在全國電視台上談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在做演說的電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrusssert , 前主持人 " 遇見新聞 " 時 , 是在談我的寫作 , 當時我住在沃爾瑪市停車場的旅行車裡 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑是因為它到了哪裡 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	然後我站在那裡 。 然後我重新讀了我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回了田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友一起住在旅行車和沙發衝浪之間 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	到了隔年的夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得了獎項 。 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人 , 全職兼職 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續污名化並犯罪化生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸 , 主要還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇過一個 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以戰勝任何事物 , 如果有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡做無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來這裡鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個你認識的乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡 , 他們在哪裡睡覺 , 或是他們在任何時間所處的生活情境 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在一個沃爾瑪超市的停車場裡 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , 梅秋.維拉維拉迪亞 , 帶我們走過全國大膽的計劃 , 提高生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多坦白、好笑 , 且非常有效的談到保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	梅秋.維拉迪達:保險套先生如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	當我還是個40年前的年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫或貧窮減少計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕婦兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:到孩子那裡 , 去找母親 , 然後跟上家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的情況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個小孩成長率極高 , 佔3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女們說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來開藥片 。 」 我們有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把 「 不 」 當作答案 ; 我們把 「 不 」 視為一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 在解釋如何使用藥丸時 , 做得很棒 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那真是太棒了 , 但它只涵蓋了全國20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	其他80%的人會孤單地離開他們 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找你們看到的普通人

we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂要大得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的對象是我們選的對象 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道顧客總是對的 , 且他們很棒 , 且他們自己在練習他們的家庭計畫 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥丸和保險套 , 在全國各個村莊 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 就這樣 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的成因的人 , 成為解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡有人--你都可以看到和婦女一起搭船 , 賣東西--這裡是浮動的市場賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 何不去宗教呢 ? 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會的教會相當強烈 , 泰國人民也是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 聽著 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裡是藍色的 , 而不是拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶把聖水灑在藥丸和保險套上 , 讓家族的清潔性 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片傳遍全國 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以 , 村落中的一些僧侶自己也在做同樣的事 。

it's been blessed . "	已經被祝福了 。 」

and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師

over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導關於家庭計畫 , 用新的字母a、b出生、保險套、iud、v為血管切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你扔骰子的地方 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你登陸任何合適的規劃 , 你就向前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 , 前進 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 重新開始 。 」

and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在上學 。

and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久後 , 保險套就知道是女孩最好的朋友了 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會變成這樣 , 所以保險套才是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個微型信用方案 , 組織出來的女性說: 「 我們只想借給實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年 , 仍然持續進行著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真的銀行 , 但它是個基金小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來執行它 , 由村民自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能看不到泰國男子 , 總是女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每一個人 , 不論他們想要協助與否 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是在七月四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供血管切除術 , 特別是 , 美國男性到排隊前面 , 直接到大使館的住宅期間 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	這間飯店給了我們球場 , 讓它很適合的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然到了午餐時間 , 他們就說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 這一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你會得到兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物不是漢堡就是熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我以為熱狗會更有象徵意義 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	接下來是這位年輕人 , 名叫威利.波姆 , 他為美國愛滋病工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他有他的血管切除術 , 因為他的熱狗一半吃了 , 他非常高興 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多消息 , 讓一些人感到憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 。 過來 , 我會幫你們做整體的 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在所有這些情況下 , 從七個孩子變成1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂方法 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟著我們 , 或者我們跟隨可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的情況 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有很強的政府 。 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但這是每個人的工作都可以改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病開始衝擊泰國 , 我們必須停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的工作並沒有受到影響 。

so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去軍方要求借300個電台
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們擁有的比政府多 , 而且他們擁有的槍比政府多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能否幫助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據後 , 他們說: 「 是的 。 好的 。 你可以使用所有的電台、電視台 。 」

and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	而在這裡 , 每一個媒體人都必須接受愛滋病的訓練 。

so they were happy with that .	所以他們對此很滿意 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校的愛滋病教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	而這些是高中生教導高中生

and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	而這些到處教導安全性愛和愛滋病毒的女孩 , 被稱為 「 伊薩媽媽 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後再下一步
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三、四年級的孩子 , 到村子裡的每個家庭 , 整個泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病的資訊和保險套給每個家庭 , 給這些年輕孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母會反對 , 因為我們試著拯救生命 , 而這是救命者 。

and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	接著 , 我們有這位船長的保險套 , 和他的哈佛mba , 到學校和夜點 。

and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們在街上到處發放保險套 , 到處都是 。

so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察放出保險套嗎 ?

and these were the condoms that we introduced .	這些是我們引進的保險套 。
one says , " weapon of mass protection . "	一個說: 「 大規模保護的武器 。 」
we found you know somebody here was searching for the weapon of mass destruction , but we have found the weapon of mass protection: the condom .	我們發現你知道這裡有人在尋找大規模毀滅性武器 , 但我們發現大規模防護性武器:保險套 。

and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 所以 , 我們說: 「 在橡膠我們信任 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以你可以看到 , 我們把一切加到我們的努力中 , 讓人民的生活變得更好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校都有保險套 , 因為酒精會損害判斷力 。
and then what happened ?	然後發生了什麼事 ?
after all this time , everybody joined in .	在這段時間之後 , 每個人都加入了 。
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國 , 愛滋病的新案件下降了90% , 根據世界銀行的報告 , 770萬條人命救了 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則今天不會有太多泰國人走來走去 。
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	所以它只顯示了 , 你可以做些什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	90%的資金來自泰國 。
there was political commitment , some financial commitment , and everybody joined in the fight .	有政治上的承諾 , 一些財務上的承諾 , 每個人都加入戰鬥中 。
so just don't leave it to the specialists and doctors and nurses .	所以只要不要把它留給專科醫師、醫生和護士
we all need to help .	我們都需要幫助 。
and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們得了愛滋病 , 這次不是單靠政府 , 而是和商業社群合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 也缺乏信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是由商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小商人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業企業
so , that was done .	所以 , 那是完成的 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	這筆錢從公司進入村莊 , 透過樹木移植
it's not a free gift .	而不是免費的禮物
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 錢就會進入他們的小額貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你可以借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮之中的人 , 信用的權利一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用的管道一定是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠脫離不了貧困 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你一定要接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功地做生意 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些企業:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 這是非常有趣的耐吉冰淇淋和耐吉餅乾 ; 這是耐吉贊助的村落 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止做鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	讓這些做得更好 , 因為我們能負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有絲綢 , 泰國絲綢
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們在做蘇格蘭tartans , 就像你們在左邊看到的 , 要賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先的人 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機可能會覺得像是朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你微笑一會兒 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•戴莫 , 他是智慧型手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 能在散步上移動 , 將一杯咖啡滑過桌面 , 用可編程的表達方式來回應你 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人是由你的手機所供電的 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手 , 在座有多少人家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是在座很多人

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive想解決的問題 , 就是我和其他二十位書呆子在romotive迷戀解決的問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八歲或八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 那真的是個很困難的問題 , 因為你得要建造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 它不但能負擔得起 , 它還得要是人們真的想要回家 , 還能在他們的孩子身邊做的事 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善和可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo的機器人使用的裝置你已經知道且愛你的iphone是他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一台wi-fi可得的機器人 , 能讓150美元的電腦可視化 , 這大約是過去這類機器人的成本的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物模式
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是用裝置上的錄影機來跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我向下吹 , 他會跟著我走 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會一直盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來這裡 , 他會轉向跟蹤我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 ,
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo就像一隻有自己的心智的寵物 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在任何兩個智慧設備之間傳送雙向音頻和影片 。
