we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在找各種方法來推回已知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:阿根廷有一種螞蟻群 , 現在已經傳播到每一塊大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一種自我導向的機器人科學家 , 很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命可能不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 與否 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但是我去年為這個長新聞挑選的就是這個:在月球上找到水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群在上面放置得更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或是在座的某人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡洛琳•波科展現了圖像 , 從卡西尼號航行到土星 , 把焦點放在它最大的月亮、泰坦星 , 以及冰凍土衛二上 , 這似乎是用來射擊冰的噴射流 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化 ,
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco讓我們飛往土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我將帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你我已經踏上好幾年了 , 50年前 , 人類首次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不但真的在月球上有腳 , 我們還在將機器人的太空船分散給所有行星 , 而且我們已經在小行星上登陸 , 還帶著彗星 , 在這個時點 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 前往冥王星的路上 , 前所知是一顆行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務都是一個更大的人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某件事 , 去了解我們宇宙之處 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球、地球 , 以及我們 , 如何在上面生存 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系的所有地方 , 我們可能去找尋像這樣的問題 , 都有土星 。 我們去過土星 , 在1980年代早期造訪過土星之前 , 土星的調查已經更加深入 , 自從卡西尼號太空船開始 , 穿越星際空間七年 , 在2004年的夏天 , 進入土星軌道 , 成為人類最遠在太陽系最高點的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞察力 , 且顯然超越了對比 , 對於這個系統的調查已經有了巨大的宇宙範圍 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就能夠學到很多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的圖片是andromedanebula , 它是我們最接近、最大型的螺旋星系 , 到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這裡有一塊美麗的旋渦星系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程 , 其實是一部分 , 也是人類旅程更大的比喻 , 來了解我們周遭所有事物的相互連結性 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位我們和卡西尼一起學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看我們過去兩年半拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我就是沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我要集中在兩個最令人興奮的故事中 , 在這次重大探索的探險探險中 , 我們正在圍繞著土星 , 已經有兩年半的時間了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著一個非常大且多樣化的衛星 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的尺寸從幾公里寬 , 大到全美這麼大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們所拍攝的土星大部分美麗的照片 , 事實上 , 都是土星和它的衛星 , 這是土星 , 土星上有dione , 然後 , 土星上展示了環形邊緣 , 展示了它們的垂直薄度 , 和月亮土衛二一樣 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47個衛星中有兩個是探測者 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛六 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裡之前 , 是太陽系中最大的一個未被探索的地形擴張 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	而這個身體已經有很長的感動人士觀看了行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像是我們在地球上的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 比起太陽系中的任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層很大 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸的分子一樣 , 只是它的大氣層被一些簡單有機物質困擾 , 如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷等 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些在土衛六的大氣層中高度的分子會被分解掉 , 它們的產品會結合在一起 , 製造出霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種迷宮無所不在 , 完全是全球化和全面性的霸主 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你不能用我們的眼睛在看得見的光譜上看到表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒 , 在我們到達卡西尼號之前 , 經過數十億年 , 溫和地漂移到水面上 , 並將表面覆蓋在厚厚的有機液體中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以像泰坦一樣 , 泰坦等於焦油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六表面溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要將水帶到地球上的 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可凝聚的 , 所以意識到這種情況會帶到一個奇特的可能性世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲之上 , 你有上百公里長的霧氣 , 防止任何陽光到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但 , 儘管有那麼冷 , 可能會有雨落在土衛六的表面 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	而在土衛六上 , 雨在地球上做些什麼 , 它會雕刻出海溝 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石坑中游泳 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把水泥沖掉高山峰和山丘 , 沖到低地 。 停下來 , 想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 土衛六上的中午和地球上深處過渡的地球一樣深 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很焦慮 , 很錯 , 很可能在下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖的岸邊 , 用油漆薄薄 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號之前就看到土衛六表面的景象 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上的發現 , 雖然在細節上並不相同 , 和故事一樣令人著迷 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼族人──那就像是胡爾斯•凡爾納冒險成真 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚、很廣的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是泰坦的照片 , 來自太陽的背景 , 背景是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	還有另一個月球 , 我甚至不知道是哪一個 。 這是個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器 , 它能透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 這大約是為我們帶來的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在太神秘了:我們無法弄清楚我們在土衛六上看到的是什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細觀察這個區域時 , 你會開始看到像我們不知道的單頻道一樣的東西 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上是一個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面卻很少有隕石坑 , 意思是說它是很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	而有些特徵看起來是構造的 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來像被拉開一樣 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到某個星球上有任何線性的東西時 , 就意味著有一個裂痕 , 就像斷層一樣 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	因此 , 它已經在板塊上改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一場事件 , 許多人被視為卡西尼調查土衛六的路燈 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲建造的惠更斯號探測器 , 卡西尼號已經運行了七年 , 遍及太陽系 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩小時半的時間 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這是多麼重要的一件事 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外太陽系著陸 , 這是人類史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這實在是太重大了 , 在我心中 , 這是個事件 , 該被讚頌在美國和歐洲各個城市的滴答帶遊行 , 可悲的是 , 並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是很重大的一個原因 。 這是國際化的使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國被慶祝 , 而慶祝的簡報是用英語、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利語、荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是關於 「 聯合國 」 這個詞的一個動人的示範 , 應該指的是:一個真正的聯合國 , 加入大規模的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探索一個行星是非常大的必要之處 , 為了了解一個行星系統 , 人類的歷史是不可收拾的 , 而現在人類已經觸及了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我只是在談這件事 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是一個極大的情緒事件 , 這是我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但無論如何 , 探測器在降落過程中對大氣進行了測量 , 它也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 從探測器上看到土衛六表面的第一張照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是令人震驚 , 因為我們希望這些其他照片從軌道上拍下來 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是一種不明確的模式 , 一種地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種垂直的排水模式 , 只能由液體的流動而形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以跟蹤這些通道 , 你可以看到它們是如何匯合在一起的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們會匯集到這裡的通道 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像一條海岸線
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是8公里的照片 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是一個航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機飛越美國 , 你就會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在鐵達尼亞航空的窗口飛越土衛六表面時所看到的 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在表面上休息 , 我要展示給各位看 , 各位先生女士 , 這是第一張從外太陽系外行星表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰卵石 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們降落的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的下面基本上就是土衛六相當於一片泥土 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個沒有鞏固的地面 , 被液態甲烷給困住了 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	很有可能 , 這種材料已經被清洗掉土衛六的高地 , 透過我們所看到的這些管道 , 排乾了數十億年 , 來填補低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 在我們的影像中 , 甚至在惠更斯的影像中 , 仍然沒有任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘高達100公尺 , 被幾公里隔開 , 延續好幾英里、幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	數百、高達一千或一百、兩百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再次感到困惑的是 , 沒有液體的屍體 , 直到最後 , 我們在極地看到了湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在土衛六的南極區有一片湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	和安大略湖的大小差不多 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過了土衛六的北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了一種特徵 , 大小和加州海一樣大 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 看來 , 液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節中 , 顯然是在泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 它是外星人 , 但卻像地球一樣奇怪 , 有著類似地球的地質形成 , 和一個巨大的地理多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 它只對太陽系的複雜性和豐富性產生了地球本身的衝突 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小衛星 , 大小約為土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到 , 在英國的旁邊 , 只為了向你展示大小 。 這並不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二非常白 , 非常亮 , 它的表面很明顯會因為碎片而被破壞 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的發現 , 發現在南極 , 我們看到的是南極 , 我們發現了這個裂痕的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋著 。 這些碎片覆蓋著有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個區域 , 南極區域 , 已經提升溫度 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 , 身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這跟發現地球上的南極比熱得多一樣奇怪 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍了額外的照片 , 我們發現從這些碎裂中 , 噴射出很好的冰粒 , 延伸出數百英里的空間 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像彩色編碼出來時 , 要帶出微弱的光線 , 我們看到這些噴射流會餵飽一團 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 我們看到 , 在土衛六上方數千英里的空間 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊對這樣的影像進行了檢查 , 就像這張 , 思考過卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是 , 這些噴射流可能從土衛二表面下的液態水袋中噴發出來 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能是液態水 , 有機物質和過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代星球探索的聖杯 , 或者 , 換句話說 , 一個可能適合生命有機體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們在我們的太陽系其他地方 , 生命的發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明基因的發生不只一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 根據推斷 , 它發生了相當驚人的次數 , 在整個宇宙和它的137億年歷史中 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是我們所知唯一仍有生命存在的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 它仍然是我們唯一知道的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代有警戒和一致性 , 我們會原諒你 , 如果你沒有 , 好吧 , 你會記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人所拍攝的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空拍攝地球 , 它對我們在宇宙中的地點有著巨大的影響 , 我們對地球保護的責任的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼號拍了相當先進的照片 , 一張前所未見的人類眼睛照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是日全食 , 從土星的另一端看過 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可能美麗的圖片中 , 你看到太陽的主要光環 , 你看到太陽的折射圖像 , 你看到這個光環 , 事實上 , 是由土衛二的表面所產生的 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 彷彿那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中發現 , 我們自己的星球的景象 , 擠在土星光環的手臂中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件很深刻的事 , 就是要從外太空看我們自己 , 並捕捉到我們在其他世界的小藍色小星球的視野 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	那 , 以及我們從中獲得的自我的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這次探索旅程得到的最佳獎勵 , 是在半個世紀前開始的 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年時 , 全世界只有15%的人被繪製 。 這會減緩一場災難後的援助遞送 , 並隱藏了未使用的土地和未知的道路的經濟潛力 。 在這場演講中 , google的laliteshkatragadademos製作人 , 一個全球各地人們用來繪製他們的世界地圖的群體地圖工具 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	laliteshkatragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 塞克隆納吉斯毀壞了緬甸人 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人並供應給這個地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 無法協助接觸周邊受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 在2005年 , 全世界只有15%的地理位置被描繪成可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國的執行總部解決了世界上大部分人口普遍面臨的問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但協助就要來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40位志工用了一個新軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路、三千間醫院、物流和解藥 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項科技 , 賦予我們每個人在地圖上所知的科技 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業 , 還有影像商店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名hernandodesto認定大部分開發中國家經濟利益的關鍵在於將大量未經處理的土地
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	例如 , 光是在印度 , 就有一兆美金的房地產沒有被考慮到 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 在170個國家 , 數以千計的使用者就已經繪製出了數百萬筆資訊 , 創造出了一幅從未思考過的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這是由各地熱情使用者的力量所構成的 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看目前使用者製作的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 在我們說話的同時 , 人們在這個170個國家的地圖上繪製了世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	還有 , 離家近一點 , chalua , 是班加羅爾的n.g路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何、手勢辨識的結果 , 以及機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數千名使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們70%未開發的星球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 布德鲁斯村的巴勒斯坦發起了一場十個月的非暴力抗議 , 阻止一場橫跨他們橄欖爐的障礙 。 你聽過嗎 ? 不這麼想 。 巴西電影製作人朱麗亞•巴查卡問過為什麼我們只關注以色列衝突中的暴力 , 而不是在有一天可能帶來和平的非暴力領導人 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力行為
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖鑄造一個龐大的國家非暴力運動來結束佔領並在該地區建立和平
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分歧在國外發生的事和認知之間是其中一個關鍵原因為什麼我們還沒有一個巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動已經成功的原因
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來這裡是要談論關注的力量 , 你的關注的力量 , 以及非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 在西岸、加薩及其他地方 , 但今天 , 我的個案研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 對於非暴力發展 , 大部分缺少的 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是為了我們開始注意那些已經是的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	容我說明一下這一點 , 讓我帶你們到這個叫做布德鲁斯村莊 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個分隔障礙 , 這個障礙的一部分會建在村落頂端 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍著 , 所以他們會失去西岸其他地方的自由權 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導 , 他們發起了一場和平抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們對於實際地面上的樣子有一種概念 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆將與以色列分離巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村這裡 , 我們了解到牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:圍籬事實上已經創造出了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被以色列兄弟姐妹加入了數十位 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列激進分子:沒有什麼比非暴力反對軍隊更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試著推動士兵 , 但沒有一個人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須要把我們對傳統思維的空虛化思想 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們正處於完全和諧狀態 , 我們想要把它散播到全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊天:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和熱門前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:圍籬的衝突持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是現場的子彈
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	像是furujah , 到處拍攝
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列激進分子:我確信我們都會死去 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但我身邊還有其他人 , 甚至沒有在牛 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	沒有需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊天:我們辦得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴查亞:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體失敗報導七年前、2003年發生的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 在十個月的和平抗爭後 , 說服了以色列政府 , 將圍牆的路線從他們的土地上移開 , 到綠線上 , 也就是國際認可了以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭從此蔓延到西岸 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦鄰里 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體大多對這些故事保持沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會造成深遠的後果 , 對於非暴力行為能夠成長的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存的可能性 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有非常重要的共通點 , 兩者都是劇場中尋求觀眾的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的演員是唯一不斷地取得封面的人 , 並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 對於非暴力的領導人 , 變得非常困難 , 讓公民不服從是可行的選擇 , 來處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量 , 可能不會讓房間裡的父母感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓孩子拋出越來越大聲的手法是給予他注意力 , 讓他第一次拋出符號 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	童年時期的心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以激勵或激勵行為 , 單單是給予孩子或給予孩子注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以受到影響 , 取決於國際社群選擇聚焦在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東衝突的核心 , 並帶來和平 , 是要我們把非暴力行為轉變為一種功能性行為 , 做法是讓更多注意到現今在地上的非暴力領袖 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我拍攝的過程中 , 在西岸、加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落中 , 我看到即使是一部紀錄片也能影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉雅吉的村落中 , 它非常靠近耶路撒冷 , 這個社區正面臨著和布德鲁斯村非常類似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 且沒有取得自由 , 要不就是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們都在使用非暴力手段 , 但自從沒有人注意到他們就變得不可思議了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一個篩選
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最有利、最有紀律的示範 , 來到約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德鲁斯村的故事 , 被記錄在影片中 , 感覺到 , 的確有人在追隨他們在做什麼 , 有人在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列一邊 , 有一個新的和平運動叫做sollidariot , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領導者一直在用布德鲁斯村作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導以色列人從來沒有過活躍過 , 在看電影時 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉吉和固體運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小預算的獨立製片也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉化為一種功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週發生的非暴力演示 , 在村落中發生的 , 像是比利•哈林、尼林、瓦拉雅、耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 如謝赫•傑拉和西爾瓦爾 , 非暴力領導人會在他們的作品中變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不去注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 彷彿它們從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我已經親眼見到如果有的話 , 它們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力終於能夠解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方工作
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意 , 讓他們可以證明它到處可行 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•塞克有一個簡單但強大的模式 , 為激勵人心的領導一切都從黃金圈開始 , 並且問 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果 , 馬丁•路德•金 , 和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•塞克:偉大領袖如何激發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們所假設的一樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠實現那些看似會違反所有假設的事 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有他們的競爭對手都要創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金恩領導了民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受過普及權利折磨的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一的偉大演說者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控權力的男子飛行 , 當肯定有其他隊伍更有資格、更有資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現權力的男子飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我做了一項發現
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深改變了我對世界運作的看法 , 它甚至深深改變了我在其中運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大、有啟發性的領導者和組織 , 不論是蘋果電腦、馬丁路德金恩或萊特兄弟──他們都這麼認為、行動 , 並用同樣的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且完全與其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是把它編碼出來 , 很可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠啟發其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼辦到的 , 不管你怎麼稱呼它為你不同的價值主張、你的專屬過程 , 或你的用戶流程 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做這些事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	藉由 「 為什麼 」 , 我指的不是 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	說到 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式、行為的方式、溝通的方式 , 都來自外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這是顯而易見的 。 我們從最清楚的東西到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞人心的領導者和激勵人心的組織 , 不論它們的大小 , 不論它們的產業全部都思考、行動 , 並從內部溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 且大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 一則行銷訊息可能會聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮的設計 , 簡單的使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? " 嗯 。 "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷都是這樣做的 , 大部分的銷售都是這樣完成的 , 大部分的人際交流就是這樣 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票之類的 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師 , 擁有最大的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶而表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它能取得很棒的氣體哩程表 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果電腦實際上是這樣傳達的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信去挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓產品有美好的設計 , 簡單的使用和使用者友好 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是剛好做出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	對嗎 ? 你準備要向我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼要做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都能完全舒適地從蘋果電腦購買電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒適地從蘋果電腦購買mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區分它們的結構性和它們的競爭者不同 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造所有這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們有資格製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在製作平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾帶著mp3播放器和pdas , 他們做出了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美設計的產品 , 沒有人買的 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從迪爾買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼要買電腦公司的mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和每個需要你的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都建立在生物學的基礎上 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的橫切面 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦其實是分成三個主要元件 , 和黃金圈完美相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 會對應到 「 什麼 」 等級 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦新皮質負責所有我們理性、分析的想法和語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間的兩個部分構成了我們的邊緣頭腦 , 我們的邊緣頭腦負責所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 而且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、益處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它就是沒有驅使行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通時 , 我們直接和大腦控制行為的部位交談 , 接著我們允許人們用我們說和做的事合理化它 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候 , 你可以給別人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節怎麼說 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那個動詞 , 它沒有 「 感覺 」 對嗎 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的那部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們能提高的最好是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你說你帶著你的心 , 或帶著你的靈魂來領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭把它打破給你們 , 那些不是身體的其他部分在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策而非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼要做你做的事 , 大家會回應為什麼你要做的事 , 那你要如何讓別人投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或更重要的是 , 忠誠和想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你擁有的東西的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是僱用需要工作的人 , 而是僱用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這樣說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人們只是因為他們可以做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們會用血汗和淚水為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子了
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人並不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求有權勢的人飛行就像是當天的點頭com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley所說的 , 我們假設的 , 是成功的秘方 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品 , 或為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你相同的三個因素:低估了 , 錯誤的人 , 市場條件不好 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是一樣的三樣東西 , 所以讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley由戰爭部門給予五萬美金以找出這台飛行機器
money was no problem .	錢根本沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉行了一個座位 , 在史密森尼時期工作 , 非常緊密 ; 他知道當時所有的大心智 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的心靈金錢 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都在為langley著想 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那我們為什麼從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley呢 ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠 , 位於俄亥俄州、奧維爾和威爾堡萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的訣竅 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用自行車商店的成績來支付他們的夢想 ; 在萊特兄弟的團隊中 , 沒有任何一個人接受大學教育 , 甚至不是奧維爾或威爾布爾 ; 而紐約時報卻無處可去 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同之處在於 , 奧維爾和威爾堡是由一個目標所驅動的 , 一個目的 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能弄清楚這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他想成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看吧 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想與他們一起工作的人 , 和血汗、淚水一起工作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他的只為支付費用
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說故事 , 故事是每次萊特兄弟出去時 , 他們都得要拿五組零件 , 因為那是他們出去買餐前撞車的次數 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟搭飛機 , 甚至沒有人在那裡經歷 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley的動機是錯的:萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是驚人的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談論你所相信的 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的 「 創新的散播法則 」 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%人口是我們早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數 , 晚期的大多數和你的房間 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式手機的唯一原因 , 是因為你不能再買輪子手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都待在不同時間點 , 在這個規模上 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不可能擁有它 , 直到你達到了這15%到18%的市場滲透點 , 然後系統就會尖端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新商業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你: 「 喔 , 大約是10% 。 」 很驕傲地 ,
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓超過百分之十的客戶絆倒 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約百分之十的 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 找到那些拿到的人 , 而不是那些拿不到的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	就是這個 , 你必須關閉的這個小缺口 , 如同jeffreymoore稱它為 「 穿越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數人不會嘗試 , 直到別人先嘗試它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很自在地做出那些腸子的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們比較自在地做出那些直覺性的決定 , 由他們所相信的這個世界所驅動 , 而不僅僅是產品所能取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在隊伍裡 , 花了六個小時買一支iphone , 當他們剛出櫃時 , 下週可以走進店裡 , 買下架一個 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些是花了四萬美金在平面電視上的人 , 他們剛出爐時 , 即使技術是次等的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為技術太棒了 , 他們自己也這麼做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要成為第一名
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 以及你做什麼 , 只要證明你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	這個人在頭六小時買iphone的原因是 , 排隊排隊六個小時 , 是因為他們相信這個世界 , 以及他們希望每個人都能看到他們:他們是第一名的 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	所以 , 讓我舉一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及一個有名的成功 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同前面說的 , 一秒鐘前 , 成功的秘訣是金錢、對的人、對的市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你當時應該有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從tivo的八、九年前到今日 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下交易 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常富有資金 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件太棒了 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我經常把東西綁在垃圾時間華納dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是商業上的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股價大約是30或40美金 , 然後跌跌倒 , 從來沒有在10美金以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至在6歲以上交易 , 除了幾個小棘手 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 可以暫停現場電視、跳過廣告、改造現場電視 , 並記住你的觀看習慣 , 連你都不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 , 我們不喜歡
you're scaring us . "	你嚇壞了我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你人生的各個面向的人 , 男孩 , 我們有產品為你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 而你所做的只是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 去聽金恩博士的演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有發出任何邀請函 , 也沒有網站可以查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	恩 , 金恩博士不是美國唯一一個很棒的演說者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個受苦於公民權利的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法是不好的
but he had a gift .	但他有個禮物
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走動 , 告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的人們採取了他的成因 , 他們讓它成為了他們自己的 , 他們告訴了人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人可以說出這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	注意 , 有25萬人出現在對的日子裡 , 聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	正是他們對美國的信念 , 讓他們可以在公車上旅行八小時 , 在八月中央站在華盛頓的陽光下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	那是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種法律:那些由更高權威製造的 , 以及由人類製造的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由人類制定的法律都和更高權威所制定的法律一致 , 我們才會活在一個公平的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好民權運動是最適合幫助他帶來他生命的起因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽聽現在的政治人物 , 帶著他們全面性的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們不鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導的人卻激勵了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們都會追隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	就是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 有能力激發他們周圍的人 , 或找到激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼還記得你把車停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是朝著正確的方向移動的 ? 神經科學家尼爾•布洛吉斯研究了我們身邊空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在大型停車場 , 我們怎麼記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬所面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	並試著去了解他大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 以黃色表示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那裡受損 , 就像阿茲海默症 , 你無法記住東西包括你把車停在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是用拉丁文來命名為 「 海馬 」 , 它的名字很相似 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以 , 人類的大腦中有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元彼此溝通的方式是發送小脈衝或刺激 , 透過彼此連結而傳遞訊息 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成 , 相互連結的密度非常高 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 做法是從老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元記錄下 , 在覓食或探索一個環境中尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以我們會想像我們從這隻老鼠的海馬體上記錄下來的一個神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當電力激發時 , 會有紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是 , 這種神經元知道每當老鼠在牠的環境中進入一個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送小型電波刺激訊號到大腦的其他部位
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以將神經元的發射率視為動物所在位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物進入其環境中的不同部位時 , 不同的神經元會發出火聲 , 就像這個正方形的箱子顯示出來的一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們一起為大腦留下了一張地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要大腦監測的電流活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	這些病人當中有些玩電玩遊戲 , 他們開車繞著一個小鎮 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	每當他們開車經過一個特定的地點時 , 就會發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人在其環境中的哪個位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方的那隻喜歡在老鼠盒子的牆壁中間射出火 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你擴大箱子時 , 發射位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那一面 , 每當有一面牆靠近南邊時 , 就喜歡開火 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞會在兩個地方發射 , 不論在哪裡有一面牆到南邊 , 當動物在盒子裡探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	這預測了你周圍的界限和方向 , 延伸到建築物等等 , 對海馬體特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入值上 , 細胞會被找到哪個專案計畫到海馬體上 , 它的確會針對特定距離或邊緣去偵測到特定距離的界線和方向 , 當老鼠在探索時 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近牆壁時 , 會發射出火 , 不論是邊緣 , 或是方方框的牆壁 , 或是圓形的牆壁 , 或圓形的牆壁 , 或甚至桌子邊緣的滴答聲 , 都是動物跑來跑去的 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發射 , 不論是南邊有界線 , 不論是桌子邊緣、牆壁 , 或甚至兩張桌子間的隔閡都會被拉開 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式 , 決定動物在探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們還可以測試我們認為物品的位置 , 比如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境或你的車會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放到他們認為旗幟或車子的位置上 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你看到旗子的位置在一個小方形的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但是你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗子的位置完全相同 , 讓位置細胞激發出來 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你記得旗幟的位置 , 透過儲存位置細胞的模式 , 來回移動位置 , 讓你最好符合你位置細胞的激發模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那引導你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過移動的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們把路徑放開 , 或許我們會停下來 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們就能整合這條路 , 大約是回頭的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從所謂的網格細胞中得到這種路徑整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞在海馬體上找到它們有點像位置細胞
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個個別的細胞都會在不同的位置發射 , 這些位置會在一個非常規律的三角網格中呈現出來 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾種網格細胞記錄下來 , 每個細胞都有像網格的圖案 , 在整個環境中 , 會產生類似的圖案 , 且每個細胞的網格格格格格狀圖案 , 會稍微偏移到其他細胞中 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	這張圖上的紅色是綠色的 , 上面是藍色的 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 把老鼠放在一起 , 好像老鼠可以在環境中發射出網格 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長距離線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳到下一個細胞來追蹤它的所在位置 , 這樣它可以利用它自己的動作來知道它在其環境中的哪個位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有類似網格的發射模式都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的電網在橘色的角度顯示 , 這意味著在大腦中特定的網格細胞的淨活性活動應該會改變 , 根據我們是否沿著六個方向跑 , 或是沿著六個中間的六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放在核磁共振掃描儀中 , 讓他們做個小小的電玩遊戲 , 像我剛剛給你們看的那個 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人類的前腦皮質中也看到了 , 這和你在老鼠身上看到的電網細胞是一樣的 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他大概還記得他的車在距離和方向上的位置 , 可以在他停車的地方附近延伸建築物和界線 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被邊界偵測細胞所呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園裡取出的路徑 , 會在電網細胞的發射中呈現出來 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都能讓位置細胞被激發
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他移動的位置 , 找到最好的位置 , 符合他大腦中位置細胞的發射模式 , 目前他停車的地方有儲存模式 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個不尊重視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被風吹過了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去拿它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找像這樣的網格激發模式 , 我們會看到它在一系列的位置 , 在我們進行各種自傳式記憶任務時 , 總是很活躍 , 比如 , 記住你上次去參加婚禮時 ,
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以可能是 , 呈現我們周遭空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重現空間的景象 , 至少 , 在我們想想像的時候發生在我們身上的事件中 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生這種事 , 你的記憶可以從細胞互相啟動 , 通過這些密集的連結 , 然後重新啟動邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個視角點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種我還沒提到的頭部導向細胞 , 它們就像指南針一樣 , 根據你所面臨的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義觀看方向 , 你想要為你的視覺圖像產生一個圖像 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮上發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以 , 這只是一個新時代的例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 比如你如何記住、想像 , 甚至思考 , 用數十億個神經元組成我們的大腦所做的動作 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全驅動的動力 , 由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾的合作所驅動 。 這不僅僅是開放原始碼電扇的遙遠希望 , 是詹姆斯•斯塔維迪斯的願景 , 也是nato的最高指揮官 , 他在近期的軍事歷史中 , 分享了鮮活的時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 應該用橋樑而不是牆壁來建造 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放原始碼、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯塔維里迪斯:北約塔最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我會講一點開放式安全因為我們必須在21世紀的安全上變得更好
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 讓我們回到二十世紀 , 有點像是了解安全風格對我們是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場位於比利時總部北部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年的verdun , 超過300天的時間 , 70萬人被殺害 , 所以大約一天2 , 000人死亡 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它向前推進20世紀的安全性進入第二次世界大戰 , 你看到史達林畢業的戰役 , 300天 , 2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝戰 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬吉諾鐵線 , 然後進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天對我們提出的論點是 , 與其建造牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是一座在歐洲著名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是dina河的橋樑 , 是ivoandri這本小說的主題 , 它談到 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹地區 , 隨著時間過去 , 已經有了巨大的建物 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫著 , 要團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會說 , 同樣地 , 開放原始碼的安全是把國際、介入、私人共和國 , 和策略性溝通連結在一起 , 主要是在社交網絡中 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物以各種方式受到攻擊 , 沒有任何對全球公有物造成威脅的來源 , 會透過建造牆壁來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條直線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	沿著它的側邊有音樂會電線 ,
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	也就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是全世界非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也非常活躍在馬拉卡的海峽
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	活躍於幾內亞灣
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球運輸系統中 , 它是十億美元的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500名海軍陸戰警舉辦人質 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海域 , 網路海域 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩位年輕男子的照片
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們指揮了一個信用卡詐欺案 , 將他們網絡超過一百億美元 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分這是全球經濟2兆美元的不連續性
two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	那只是在英國的國內生產總值下 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這種無止境的網路海 , 我們所知的根本性開放性 , 也非常受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事 , 是人口販賣造成的威脅 , 是毒品、鴉片 , 從阿富汗出來 , 透過歐洲來到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從安地斯山北邊來的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和人口販賣的運動 。 最重要的是 , 也許 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它所需的糟糕成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販子大多在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位 , 這是一塊非常高科技的美國海軍艦隊 , 我們用它來阻止販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是毒品卡特爾的半潛水員 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	建在南美洲叢林裡
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的木筏抓到它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個組員 。 精密的溝通打掃了 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣 , 在毒品、在人、在武器、上帝禁止 , 在大規模破壞的武器中 , 是對全球公有物造成威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	今天讓我們一起在阿富汗
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是在阿富汗的一塊大便領域 。
